<span id="freeTextContainer11629474836447413837">I read Peter Pan for the first time about five years ago, aloud to my kids. They couldn't follow it, I thought it was okay. It was a paperback with the movie tie-in cover. Then I saw this gorgeous, illustrated, three-dimensional version at Costco and thought, Ah, why not? The "Pan" movie is coming out, my kids love the Tinker Bell movies on Disney Channel, they might as well see what started it all. <br /><br />I really loved this. There's something about having illustrations, and little quotes picked out f</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11629474836447413837">I read Peter Pan for the first time about five years ago, aloud to my kids. They couldn't follow it, I thought it was okay. It was a paperback with the movie tie-in cover. Then I saw this gorgeous, illustrated, three-dimensional version at Costco and thought, Ah, why not? The "Pan" movie is coming out, my kids love the Tinker Bell movies on Disney Channel, they might as well see what started it all. <br /><br />I really loved this. There's something about having illustrations, and little quotes picked out from the chapters as headers, that really makes the story come clear in your head. The kids loved it, and not just because of the fold out maps and compasses, but they followed the story (they were too young before) and they enjoyed the story. Also, this version has notations defining old-fashioned words or idioms, which was great. </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/10756459-peter-pan" title="Leather Bound 9781435133471" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a href="/review/list/4327582-rikke?shelf=childrens-books" class="actionLinkLite">childrens-books</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer428631125">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9644096676409891025">“<em>All children, except one, grow up.</em>” <br /><br />Thus begins the most classic piece of children's literature of all-time. Written with such delicate embellishments the language is a wonder in itself, and you will find yourself sighing with delight at the stunning metaphors and fanciful explanations. <br />The story is naturally as immortal as Peter Pan himself, and every child should have the pleasure of taking off to Neverland along with him. Neverland is the perfect idealization of every child's imaginative dre</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9644096676409891025">“<em>All children, except one, grow up.</em>” <br /><br />Thus begins the most classic piece of children's literature of all-time. Written with such delicate embellishments the language is a wonder in itself, and you will find yourself sighing with delight at the stunning metaphors and fanciful explanations. <br />The story is naturally as immortal as Peter Pan himself, and every child should have the pleasure of taking off to Neverland along with him. Neverland is the perfect idealization of every child's imaginative dreamland - complete with mermaids, fairies, pirates, indians and infinite adventures. As a child I wished desperately for Peter Pan to show up at my window and whisk me away.<br /><br />"<em>The moment you doubt whether you can fly, you cease for ever to be able to do it.</em>"<br /><br />And yet the story is so melancholic and so heartbreakingly sad. There's a subtle tone of tragedy to the character of Peter Pan, which I never detected as a child. His longing for a mother and his lack of belonging and attachment is actually turning him into the most lonely boy in the world. In some ways he resembles Antoine de Saint-Exupery's Little Prince in his isolation.<br />This is so much more than a mere lullaby for children, it is a complex story with many layers - written for adults as well as children.<br /><br />"<em>Stars are beautiful, but they may not take part in anything, they must just look on forever.</em>"</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_227275054">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/227275054" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan" class="left imgcol" title="Jonathan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1450116936p2/6313408.jpg" alt="Jonathan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/227275054?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 23, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6313408-jonathan" class="user" title="Jonathan">Jonathan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Hardcover 9780805072457" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=personal-favourites" class="actionLinkLite">personal-favourites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=classic-literature" class="actionLinkLite">classic-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=children-s-literature" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-literature</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=childhood-book" class="actionLinkLite">childhood-book</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=re-read" class="actionLinkLite">re-read</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/6313408-jonathan?shelf=classic-challenge-2" class="actionLinkLite">classic-challenge-2</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer227275054">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer270209190986746980"><br /><em>Peter Pan</em> is the classic tale of the boy who never grew up. In essence one could take this as a metaphor for immaturity, for there is certainly a difference between any man aging physically, mentally or emotionally. In my re-reading of this novel, I found that this theme stood out to me a lot more, along with several other, more sinister themes regarding parenthood and social acceptability. The overall message conveyed by Barrie appears to be one of conformity, not one of self discovery. Yet thi</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText270209190986746980"><br /><em>Peter Pan</em> is the classic tale of the boy who never grew up. In essence one could take this as a metaphor for immaturity, for there is certainly a difference between any man aging physically, mentally or emotionally. In my re-reading of this novel, I found that this theme stood out to me a lot more, along with several other, more sinister themes regarding parenthood and social acceptability. The overall message conveyed by Barrie appears to be one of conformity, not one of self discovery. Yet this again is contradicted by the nature of the protagonist who crows proudly, is unafraid of danger and sees death as one 'awfully big adventure'.<br /><br />It is the whimsical nature of <em>Peter Pan</em> that leads me to allow it some leeway, despite the themes which are steeped in views and values of the times. In other words it is a book about propriety and what is right. But back to the whimsical nature of this book: I love whimsy. There is something nostalgic, magical and reminiscent of childish innocence and imagination in <em>Peter Pan</em> despite its darker themes. Have you never wished to fly, free of anything? Have you never wished to go on an adventure to strange and magical lands? Or live in a family where a dog is your nursemaid? It is these kinds of humorous, wonderful desires that <em>Peter Pan</em> reaches out to.<br /><br />It is also these desires that the protagonist Pan reaches out to when he steals away the children. And what is particular sinister here is that he steals away Wendy to make her the mother of himself and all the lost boys. But not to be a real mother, but a pretend mother. A mother who will do as he wants and be the kind of mother he desires. And of course the reader recognises that this is a wrong kind of mother-son relationship going on (for Pan cannot understand romance of course and does not see Wendy in any kind of womanly situation except as that of maternal place-holder). But in the end we also see Wendy return to society, free from the wild, and take up the place of mother again.<br /><br />I'm not at all suggesting that this is a bad thing. More that the way that Barrie paints it is imposing, limited and forceful. He suggests that one should not be a mother bound by certain restrictions and then returns Wendy to those very restrictions he claims to deny. In other words he proposes the freedom of his one female character, yet denies it with his actions. Of course, for all the reader knows Wendy I believe, chooses to become a mother and this would be a good thing. Yet it is the way, bound up in the notions of what is proper, that Barrie writes and juxtaposes the two families, that leads the reader to consider that perhaps neither family is exactly 'proper'.<br /><br />Yet, as mentioned, for all its old fashioned ideas (it is a dated classic - one of several), this novel is one which also possesses many wonderfully innocent and whimsical notions about faraway lands, adventures and magic. And for that alone I consider it a story that should be thoughtfully considered as to what it says about what is to be valued in freedom, maturity, innocence and spirit. For in many ways the story and its themes contradict one another, but in many ways they work well together as a flowing pattern.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="270209190986746980">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5782907484366151333">Might try contrasting the book with Water Babies, which was written about the same time. Water Babies deals more with lower-class children.</span>

        rated it

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer100307378">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17427022479016445858">I'll start with the cons so we can end on a happy note.<br /><br /><strong>Cons:</strong><br />This book is weird and sexist. It's been ages since I saw the Disney version, so I don't remember all those sketchy parts of the story.<br /><br /><strong>Pros:</strong><br />This is such a sweet, sad fairy tale about the pains of growing up, and at the same time it's a bittersweet love story. <br /><br />I love how flight is used as a symbol for youth:<br /><blockquote>It is sad to have to say that the power to fly gradually left them. At first Nana tied their feet to the bed-posts so that they shou</blockquote></span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17427022479016445858">I'll start with the cons so we can end on a happy note.<br /><br /><strong>Cons:</strong><br />This book is weird and sexist. It's been ages since I saw the Disney version, so I don't remember all those sketchy parts of the story.<br /><br /><strong>Pros:</strong><br />This is such a sweet, sad fairy tale about the pains of growing up, and at the same time it's a bittersweet love story. <br /><br />I love how flight is used as a symbol for youth:<br /><blockquote>It is sad to have to say that the power to fly gradually left them. At first Nana tied their feet to the bed-posts so that they should not fly away in the night; and one of their diversions by day was to pretend to fall off buses; but by and by they ceased to tug at their bonds in bed, and found that they hurt themselves when they let go of the bus. In time they could not even fly after their hats. Want of practice, they called it; but what it really meant was that they no longer believed.</blockquote><br />My favorite part of the book is the last chapter:<br />"Why can't you fly now, mother?"<br />"Because I am grown up, dearest. When people grow up they forget the way."<br />"Why do they forget the way?"<br />"Because they are no longer gay and innocent and heartless. It is only the gay and innocent and heartless who can fly."<br /><br />Magical, isn't it?<br /><br />When I become a grown-up who's no longer gay or innocent or heartless (oh, how I shudder to think!), I know I will love to reread <em>Peter Pan</em>, particularly the last chapter, for its unparalleled ability to stir up nostalgia.</span>

      <a href="/user/show/326250-kelly" class="user" title="Kelly">Kelly</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer9376964">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17257153677266304855">The last three books I finished were all trauma-related nonfiction. So one morning before work, I scanned my shelves hoping to find something I hadn't read four times already, to occupy my morning commute - something light and untraumatic. Classic fiction for children seemed like a good idea, so I pulled down this copy of Peter Pan that I've had since about fifth grade.<br /><br />I soon remembered why my fifth grade self couldn't stomach finishing even Chapter Three. By that point, Peter has managed to tur</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17257153677266304855">The last three books I finished were all trauma-related nonfiction. So one morning before work, I scanned my shelves hoping to find something I hadn't read four times already, to occupy my morning commute - something light and untraumatic. Classic fiction for children seemed like a good idea, so I pulled down this copy of Peter Pan that I've had since about fifth grade.<br /><br />I soon remembered why my fifth grade self couldn't stomach finishing even Chapter Three. By that point, Peter has managed to turn Wendy on to the idea of running away by wooing her with the prospect of darning socks and sewing pockets. And Tinker Bell has displayed shows of "womanly" jealousy towards Wendy, for stealing Peter's attentions. Barf. Suffice to say, I was not the kind of girl who could identify with these kinds of characters, let alone be wooed all the way to Chapter Four. <br /><br />Alas, my adult self is a quicker reader, and, double alas, I have a more jaded tolerance of tales of bullcrap gender stereotypes. Or at least I thought I did, until I got to the truly intolerable ending. Barf again, I say.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_133940065">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/133940065" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1470974-lynai" class="left imgcol" title="Lynai"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1386837151p2/1470974.jpg" alt="Lynai" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/133940065?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Dec 22, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1470974-lynai" class="user" title="Lynai">Lynai</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Hardcover 9780805072457" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1470974-lynai?shelf=ebook" class="actionLinkLite">ebook</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1470974-lynai?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1470974-lynai?shelf=501-childrens-books" class="actionLinkLite">501-childrens-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a onclick="Effect.toggle('reviewTextContainer133940065'); return false;" href="#">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span style="display:none" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer133940065">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13109043683022205318">I have to confess that this is the first time I have read the story although Peter Pan, Wendy, Tinkerbell and Hook are fairly familiar to me, due to the movie, Hook, which I got to watch with my siblings back in high school. It was one wonderful family bonding moment the reason why the movie stayed in my memory until now.<br /><br />Written as a children’s story, Peter Pan the novel tells of the beauty of youth and the wonders of childhood. The mermaids, fairies, and magic indeed play a great part in a chil</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13109043683022205318">I have to confess that this is the first time I have read the story although Peter Pan, Wendy, Tinkerbell and Hook are fairly familiar to me, due to the movie, Hook, which I got to watch with my siblings back in high school. It was one wonderful family bonding moment the reason why the movie stayed in my memory until now.<br /><br />Written as a children’s story, Peter Pan the novel tells of the beauty of youth and the wonders of childhood. The mermaids, fairies, and magic indeed play a great part in a child’s life and imagination. As a child, dreams were a big deal to me. Some were pleasant and some were recurring nightmares. And I had also dreamt of flying, like the flying that Wendy and her brothers did, though I had not dreamt of Neverland. Were it not that all children, at some time or another, wish they could fly? In fact, as an adult, I still dream of flying over treetops and oceans and mountains. :D<br /><br />More than a story about being a child, Peter Pan is also a story about growing up. It tells the difference between what is real and what is a fantasy. More than ever, it tells of the virtue of choice. Wendy chose to grow up, Peter chose to live as a carefree boy.<br /><br />I especially love the last chapter, “When Wendy Grew Up”. Life in its normal cycle went on for Wendy, who chose to live in reality where she grew up and had a little girl of her own, whom Peter from time to time (if he doesn’t forget!) visited and took with him to Neverland for spring cleaning. And I like how Wendy, all grown up and motherly, still has those moments where she could look back and think, with satisfaction, of what a wonderful childhood she had back then. Didn’t we all wanted to do just like that? To grow up and then look back with fondness at how we had firmly believed in fairies and magic and flying?<br /><br />My more thorough review at <a rel="nofollow" href="http://lynaireads.luigiandlynai.net/2010/12/peter-pan-j-m-barrie//"><strong>Lynaireads</strong>.</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13109043683022205318">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_285490256">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285490256" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4545538-rachel-hartman" class="left imgcol" title="Rachel Hartman"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442465555p2/4545538.jpg" alt="Rachel Hartman" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/285490256?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 28, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4545538-rachel-hartman" class="user" title="Rachel Hartman">Rachel Hartman</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Hardcover 9780805072457" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer285490256">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5385718459111481235">I just read this for the first time - can you believe it? I knew the story, of course. I saw the Disney movie way back when, and probably some spin-offs too (Hook? Was that one?). And I may even have seen the play, or part of it. But I'd never read the book itself.<br /><br />It was cute. I was really intrigued by the way the author asserts that children are wee narcissistic sociopaths - and here he is saying it right to his (young) readers' faces, confident that it will go over their heads. And I'm sure it</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5385718459111481235">I just read this for the first time - can you believe it? I knew the story, of course. I saw the Disney movie way back when, and probably some spin-offs too (Hook? Was that one?). And I may even have seen the play, or part of it. But I'd never read the book itself.<br /><br />It was cute. I was really intrigued by the way the author asserts that children are wee narcissistic sociopaths - and here he is saying it right to his (young) readers' faces, confident that it will go over their heads. And I'm sure it does. I've got an eight-year-old; I know what self-centred little monsters they can be (and know, too, that they get over it eventually. That WE get over it eventually, I should say, for we are none of us exempt).<br /><br />I loved the idea of The Neverland as something all children recognize, as imagination games made literal. I loved what an asshole Tinker Bell was, to say nothing of the mermaids. But, alas, it was really hard for me to get around all the racism and sexism. I know this book, like all books, is a product of its times, but still. My eyes got sore from rolling so hard, and that really hampers my enjoyment of a book.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5385718459111481235">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

      Becca

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/23016460-amber?shelf=tattered-tales-buddyread" class="actionLinkLite">tattered-tales-buddyread</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer781890260">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer831410052885616020">This was my first time reading the original and uncut story of Peter Pan. It was recommended to me at the All About Books Book club by one of my book club buddies there. I decided to read this after I read <a title="The Child Thief by Brom" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief">The Child Thief</a>by Brom which is my favorite version of Peter Pan so far after he said that reading this book inspired him to write The Child Thief. He said there was a line in this book that piqued his interest and that had him questioning why that happened. He wrote all about that in the afte</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText831410052885616020">This was my first time reading the original and uncut story of Peter Pan. It was recommended to me at the All About Books Book club by one of my book club buddies there. I decided to read this after I read <a title="The Child Thief by Brom" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6308379.The_Child_Thief">The Child Thief</a>by Brom which is my favorite version of Peter Pan so far after he said that reading this book inspired him to write The Child Thief. He said there was a line in this book that piqued his interest and that had him questioning why that happened. He wrote all about that in the afterword of The Child Thief. This was a pretty good read though through all it's whimsy it is much more darker and nastier than the Disney version everyone is used to. There is betrayal, selfishness, treachery, and more in this book. There are pirates fighting Indians in this book and more. It is the classic story of Peter Pan who takes Wendy, Michael, and John Darling to Neverland with a petty fairy named Tinker Belle, the Lost Boys and a tortured Pirate named Captain Hook who is scared of a crocodile that ate a clock that hungers for his flesh. All in all I enjoyed this book and would recommend this classic children's tale to all ages. This book is my second favorite Peter Pan story besides the Child Thief. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="831410052885616020">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer7925436534973188877">Barrie had me at page 1.<br />"All children, except one grow up. They soon know that they will grow up...Mrs. Darling cried,'Oh why can't you remain like this for ever!'...henceforth Wendy knew she must grow up...Two is the beginning of the end."<br />I can't believe how many children's books I read to myself and my daughter, but never Peter and Wendy, just the Golden Book of Peter Pan. This abridged edition of course, includes the main characters, Hook, Smee, Tinker Bell, the crocodile, etc. but it leaves</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7925436534973188877">Barrie had me at page 1.<br />"All children, except one grow up. They soon know that they will grow up...Mrs. Darling cried,'Oh why can't you remain like this for ever!'...henceforth Wendy knew she must grow up...Two is the beginning of the end."<br />I can't believe how many children's books I read to myself and my daughter, but never Peter and Wendy, just the Golden Book of Peter Pan. This abridged edition of course, includes the main characters, Hook, Smee, Tinker Bell, the crocodile, etc. but it leaves out Barrie's sarcastic and wise commetary.<br />The Lost Boys knew,"in what they called their hearts that one can get on quite well without a mother, and that it is only mothers who think you can't." One of the Lost Boys remembers that his mother used to ask his father for a check book of her own.<br />Peter's cockiness and crowing is a large part of his charm and also an irritant and a stumbling block to his growth and his ability to maintain relationships.<br />If you've seen Mary Martin flying to Neverland, you're probably hooked on the story, but there's so much more.</span>

  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16027395891104848566">Yo, personalmente, he crecido con las películas de Disney, y al leer las versiones originales de los cuentos, me estoy quedando un poco alucinada viendo como cambian la verdadera historia. Aunque tal vez las originales sean un poco bestias, son preferibles -a mi parecer, claro-.     <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1271361952">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1271361952" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova" class="left imgcol" title="Jeannette Nikolova"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1446376503p2/2574284.jpg" alt="Jeannette Nikolova" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1271361952?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 05, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2574284-jeannette-nikolova" class="user" title="Jeannette Nikolova">Jeannette Nikolova</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/34268.Peter_Pan" title="Hardcover 9780805072457" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1271361952">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17136446465292040739"><a rel="nofollow" href="https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2015/05/05/peter-pan-by-j-m-barrie/"> <em>Read on the WondrousBooks blog.</em> </a><br /><br /><strong>MY 1000th BOOK. I came this far only to hit the big number with a book I should have probably read in my childhood. </strong><br /><br />How often do you have the opportunity to read a story you've known your entire life for the first time? Because <em>Peter Pan</em> is part of the lives of each and every one of us, and yet, with a little shame, I admit I never really read the original novel by J.M. Barrie. I've watched every single movie made, whether it's a motion picture, an animation or e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17136446465292040739"><a rel="nofollow" href="https://wondrousbooks.wordpress.com/2015/05/05/peter-pan-by-j-m-barrie/">
  <em>Read on the WondrousBooks blog.</em>
</a><br /><br /><strong>MY 1000th BOOK. I came this far only to hit the big number with a book I should have probably read in my childhood. </strong><br /><br />How often do you have the opportunity to read a story you've known your entire life for the first time? Because <em>Peter Pan</em> is part of the lives of each and every one of us, and yet, with a little shame, I admit I never really read the original novel by J.M. Barrie. I've watched every single movie made, whether it's a motion picture, an animation or even a TV show(Once Upon a Time, but still...). I've even seen the Johnny Depp movie about Barrie himself. Yet, until today this book remained unread.<br /><p>And now it saddens me that I didn't read it as a child, because I would have loved it, as I loved the movies and animations. However, as critical and over-analyzing as I am today, I couldn't help but find some problems with this book. Honestly, I'm not even sure 3 stars is the right rating. I don't know if there is a right rating. Grading a story which has left such a mark on your life is a hard thing to do. Because I was disappointed by the book, but I have so many magical childhood memories about Peter Pan himself. But since I've promised myself to be truthful in these reviews, I'll honestly tell you the things that didn't sit right with me.<br /><br />&gt;- I'm not sure if this is the product of the fact that I'm not a child anymore, but<em> I didn't get the feeling that this was a proper children's book</em>. I actually felt that there were many sexual connotations, it was too grown up in a way, an therefore a bit disturbing.<br /><br />For one, there was<strong> Tink's attitude toward Peter</strong>, which seemed like the one of a jealous girlfriend, including her actual jealousy, and the fact that she curses a lot every time she appears, including things which are not explained, but it is made obvious that she is saying obscenities.<br /><br />Then there was<strong> the whole kissing business</strong>, obviously:<br /><img class="escapedImg" alt="" src="https://d.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1430854155ra/14770642.gif" /><br /><br />And especially: <strong>all of these kids playing at being mothers, fathers and their babies</strong>. Wendy and Peter as a couple, Wendy acting as a mother, the subtle discussions about babies and how they come to be. If this was a child's play, like children often do, it would be one thing, but this novel is written by a man who, by that point, knew perfectly well where babies come from so it seemed wrong to read the way he embeds such talk and behaviour in small children.<br /><br />- The book seemed disturbing and inappropriate in another fashion, too. Namely, <strong>all of the children become murderers at one point and that is described as no big deal</strong>. There is no moral dilemma, none of them even thinks twice about killing. I can't see in what way is it normal to take murder lightly, and I don't think it is so in most fairytales, brothers Grimm excluded, because their version today is much happier than it once was.<br /><br />- The character of Peter Pan. I was sort of surprised when I found out that he is going to be a villain in OUAT, but after reading the book now, it's actually not so hard to imagine. <strong>Peter is a volatile and egotistical character</strong>. He is bossy, and not in a nice way, and he often mistreats and humiliates his Lost boys(though I don't remember them ever being called that in the book itself). Not to mention the entire business about him escorting dead children as far as he can on their way to the other side. Which, on its own, makes me question this entire book and makes me think a lot about dead children, much as <strong>The Brothers Lionheart</strong>. But maybe getting into this would be over-thinking it, so I'll just leave it here as an idea for you too.</p></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17136446465292040739">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('hML53jQLmkawxgixYJ8gYjO+3V8yqr8FOpZ0SPBCQy7hFsYNxtmOvDwefAoe/sbQekkeRnt3+K9Qn3HaPNe1aw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('82hGYWL5n+nt1yhOgNUXNRn2iWTs2ASYurThjiSnT9iWvHmykCuLE2EPXPX+tPGHUAFKfaUFQzLQveQc6DK5nQ==')})
  }

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/5255014.J_M_Barrie">About J.M. Barrie</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/5255014.J_M_Barrie"><img alt="5255014" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1318047214p2/5255014.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer17590155394894340608">Sir James Matthew Barrie, 1st Baronet, OM (9 May 1860 – 19 June 1937) was a Scottish author and dramatist, best remembered today as the creator of <em>Peter Pan.</em><br /><br />The child of a family of small-town weavers, he was educated in Scotland. He moved to London, where he developed a career as a novelist and playwright. There he met the Llewelyn Davies boys who inspired him in writing about a baby boy who has</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17590155394894340608">Sir James Matthew Barrie, 1st Baronet, OM (9 May 1860 – 19 June 1937) was a Scottish author and dramatist, best remembered today as the creator of <em>Peter Pan.</em><br /><br />The child of a family of small-town weavers, he was educated in Scotland. He moved to London, where he developed a career as a novelist and playwright. There he met the Llewelyn Davies boys who inspired him in writing about a baby boy who has magical adventures in Kensington Gardens (included in <em>The Little White Bird</em>), then to write <em>Peter Pan, or The Boy Who Wouldn't Grow Up,</em> a "fairy play" about this ageless boy and an ordinary girl named Wendy who have adventures in the fantasy setting of Neverland. This play quickly overshadowed his previous work and although he continued to write successfully, it became his best-known work, credited with popularising the name Wendy, which was very uncommon previously.<br /><br />Barrie unofficially adopted the Davies boys following the deaths of their parents. Before his death, he gave the rights to the Peter Pan works to Great Ormond Street Hospital, which continues to benefit from them.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17590155394894340608">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/5255014.J_M_Barrie" class="actionLink moreLink">More about J.M. Barrie...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
